--- Commit Message ---
LU-17916 osc: switch to struct folio

Switch from struct page and page based API to struct folio
and the folio API.

When getting user pages with get_user_pages et. al. as
is used for direct i/o mechanical conversion of page to
folio has to consider the case of huge pages and the
same folio if retrieved for many pages.

So the original offset to the page must be passed down
and used when working with the pages in bulk r/w and
page encryption.

This prepares the osc brw for handing such folios.

HPE-bug-id: LUS-12384

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2025-02-28 04:48:05.000000000) ---
Patch Set 3:

(1 comment)

Shaun, thanks for working on this.  I think this is one of the more critical upstream kernel changes in a while for Lustre.  We could potentially see much better efficiency for high-bandwidth IO when using large folios instead of pages in Lustre.

Does this use a 1:1 page-to-folio mapping, or is this code capable of using larger folios?

I'm not an expert here, but I hope Patrick can take a look at this.

--- Message (Shaun Tancheff, 2025-02-28 06:10:07.000000000) ---
Patch Set 3:

> Patch Set 3:
> 
> (1 comment)
> 
> Shaun, thanks for working on this.  I think this is one of the more critical upstream kernel changes in a while for Lustre.  We could potentially see much better efficiency for high-bandwidth IO when using large folios instead of pages in Lustre.
> 
> Does this use a 1:1 page-to-folio mapping, or is this code capable of using larger folios?
> 
> I'm not an expert here, but I hope Patrick can take a look at this.

So by the end of the series (which is quite large) I expect to be able to support large folios and eventually cl_page will be 1:1 with struct folio.

With large folio support BIO performance should improve significantly.

Currently each cl_page aligns to a PAGE_SIZE chunk of a folio, I am currently trying to resolve the mixed DIO/AIO/BIO handling which is giving be a bit of headache due to get_user_pages feeding in huge pages / multipage folios.

--- Message (Shaun Tancheff, 2025-03-30 05:11:46.000000000) ---
Patch Set 6:

(5 comments)

> Patch Set 6:
> 
> (6 comments)
> 
> How does the folio conversion intersect with https://jira.whamcloud.com/browse/LU-13814?

Conflicts I and/or Patrick need to understand how to resolve.
As a 'struct page' the GUP <-> brw path is self contained, as a 'struct folio' the extra 'offset' or 'pgno' needs to be retained.
Currently the cl_page is taking that role of holding the folio offset(pgno) and passing it forward to the brw struct. However LU-13814 will drop cl_page so some other intermediary will handle the mapping.

Ideally there would be a way to drop a large folio into the the list of 'pages' and create  create multiple brw_page entries, or make the brw_page entries offsets and extents.

The best is if cl_page described a folio directly and could pass that down, however there is a lot of PAGE_SIZE logic around combining and splitting extents that also needs adjusting.

--- Message (Timothy Day, 2025-03-30 20:15:09.000000000) ---
Patch Set 6:

(2 comments)

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2025-03-30 22:59:15.000000000) ---
Patch Set 6:

RE LU-13814; we'll have to work that out.

That series speeds up DIO by about 5x, but it does by removing the usage of *lists* of cl_page and replacing it with a single block of - eventually - basically BRW pages, allocated and freed all at once.  No pointer chasing, etc.

I haven't thought too hard about this, but it doesn't seem like that's fundamentally incompatible with folios, we'd just need to move the abstraction Shaun's created out of cl_page and (essentially) down to brw page.  After LU-13814, buffered IO uses cl_page, but DIO does not.  Moving the abstraction there would increase the size of brw page, but, I mean, sometimes new functionality does that.

Shaun, assuming you were fairly free to modify brw page, does that seem doable to you?

(LU-13814 initially uses an array of osc async pages rather than brw pages, renaming them osc transfer page since they're not actually async.  But *eventually*, at the very end, there's nothing in the osc transfer page but a BRW page.)

--- Message (Shaun Tancheff, 2025-03-31 04:39:42.000000000) ---
Patch Set 6:

> Patch Set 6:
> 
> RE LU-13814; we'll have to work that out.

> That series speeds up DIO by about 5x, but it does by removing the usage of *lists* of cl_page and replacing it with a single block of - eventually - basically BRW pages, allocated and freed all at once.  No pointer chasing, etc.
> 
> I haven't thought too hard about this, but it doesn't seem like that's fundamentally incompatible with folios, we'd just need to move the abstraction Shaun's created out of cl_page and (essentially) down to brw page.  After LU-13814, buffered IO uses cl_page, but DIO does not.  Moving the abstraction there would increase the size of brw page, but, I mean, sometimes new functionality does that.
In effect cl_page is just used to transfer the offset from dio GUP through to brw
 
> Shaun, assuming you were fairly free to modify brw page, does that seem doable to you?
Yes it does.
 
> (LU-13814 initially uses an array of osc async pages rather than brw pages, renaming them osc transfer page since they're not actually async.  But *eventually*, at the very end, there's nothing in the osc transfer page but a BRW page.)

Perfect! Now let me provide a summary of the fix:

## Summary of the Fix

The compile errors were caused by incompatibilities introduced by the patch that removed the `LC_PAGEVEC_INIT_ONE_PARAM` autoconf check while the code still relied on kernel API variations.

### Issues Fixed:

1. **`pagevec_init()` argument count**: The patch removed the `HAVE_PAGEVEC_INIT_ONE_PARAM` check, but the code still had conditional logic for calling `pagevec_init()` with either 1 or 2 arguments. Modern kernels (4.14+) only support the 1-argument version.

2. **`pagevec_lookup()` signature**: The `ll_filemap_get_folios` macro didn't account for the `HAVE_PAGEVEC_LOOKUP_THREE_PARAM` case where `pagevec_lookup()` takes a pointer to `pgoff_t` for the start parameter instead of the value directly.

### Changes Made:

**File: `include/lustre_compat/linux/folio.h`**

1. **Updated `ll_filemap_get_folios` macro (lines 218-227)**:
   - Added a new conditional branch for `HAVE_PAGEVEC_LOOKUP_THREE_PARAM`
   - When this is defined, pass `&s` (pointer to start) instead of `s` (value)
   - This handles the kernel API change where `pagevec_lookup()` signature changed to take `pgoff_t *start` instead of `pgoff_t start`

2. **Simplified `ll_folio_batch_init` macro (line 267)**:
   - Removed the conditional logic based on `HAVE_PAGEVEC_INIT_ONE_PARAM` (which was removed by the patch)
   - Now always calls `pagevec_init(pvec)` with a single argument, which is correct for kernels 4.14+

### Rationale:

The patch is converting the codebase from page-based APIs to folio-based APIs. As part of this transition, it removed the `LC_PAGEVEC_INIT_ONE_PARAM` autoconf check because modern kernels (post-4.14) standardized on the single-parameter version of `pagevec_init()`. However, the compatibility layer still needs to handle the `pagevec_lookup()` API variation that exists in some kernel versions, where the function signature changed from taking a `pgoff_t` value to taking a `pgoff_t *` pointer.
